Shandong Province Preserves the Yang Family Collection in Liaocheng 98

The Haiyuan Pavilion of the Yang family in Liaocheng, Shandong, contains tens of thousands of volumes of books, mostly old Song and Yuan editions, meticulously copied and annotated, which are related to our country's culture and national essence. However, in recent years, due to repeated banditry, the collection has been sold off. It is heard that if no measures are taken to preserve this treasure, it will inevitably continue to be dispersed. The Provincial Department of Education, seeing this, has submitted a request to the Provincial Government to order Wang Xiantang, the director of the Provincial Library, to work with the Liaocheng County Head and local organizations to investigate the Yang family collection. The investigation has been completed. In addition to the books that have already been lost, there are still more than 200,000 volumes. Wang and others have registered them one by one. The 43rd standing meeting of the Provincial Government has decided to order the Departments of Civil Affairs and Education to jointly build the Haiyuan Pavilion in the Zhongshan Hall of the Provincial Library to preserve the collection. They have also jointly drafted temporary preservation measures to temporarily move out a suitable location in the library to purchase book boxes and shelves. Once the collection arrives, it will be stored immediately, and a detailed plan for the construction of the Haiyuan Pavilion will be actively drafted for permanent preservation.

Municipal Bureau of Education Unifies Classroom Names 102

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education issued an order to all municipal primary schools, stating: "In order to comply with the matter, we have found that the names of classrooms in municipal primary schools are inconsistent, with some using school mottoes and others using personal names. In order to unify the names of classrooms in all schools, the classrooms should be named after the grades in the classroom. If the classroom is a single-grade classroom, it should be named Spring First Classroom, Autumn First Classroom, etc. If the classroom is a multi-grade classroom, it should be named Spring One-Two Classroom, Autumn One-Two Classroom, etc. If it is a single-grade classroom, it should be referred to as Classroom for short. Other classrooms can be named analogously." The bureau hereby orders all municipal primary schools to comply and implement this order.

Municipal Bureau of Education Convenes a Meeting with Principals of Private Secondary Schools 103

March 22nd

The Municipal Bureau of Education issued an order to all schools yesterday, stating: "In order to comply with the matter, it is necessary for schools to understand each other's operating conditions and for the administrative agencies of education to understand each other's administrative policies so that improvement is easier and development is faster. Our bureau previously convened a meeting with the principals of municipal schools to communicate opinions and discuss important matters. It is urgent to continue holding such meetings for private schools. It is now scheduled to convene the first meeting of principals of private secondary schools at 1:00 PM on March 22nd at our bureau. The meeting will report on the administrative policies of our bureau for private secondary schools that have been registered and the work we plan to do recently. The principals can report in detail on the actual situation of each school, such as the organization of grades, the general economic situation, development plans, and difficulties. The meeting will also discuss issues such as the standards for students to pay various fees, strict enrollment of transfer students, and the organization of public science laboratories. The deadline for collecting proposals from each school is March 17th. Each principal or director should attend on time to discuss the issues together. This order is hereby issued to the school for compliance."

The Preparatory Office announced that, because the number of athletes from various provinces and cities who have telegraphed to participate has reached more than 2,000, preparations for the athletes' food and accommodation have been completed.

Dormitories: The dormitories prepared by the association are the former barracks, divided into three large rooms. The address is across from the Games venue, with fresh air and enough space for more than 2,000 people. Each large room is divided into more than 20 small rooms, and each small room can accommodate more than 30 people. Each room is equipped with two electric lights, and there are attached washing areas, bathrooms, and toilets that have been arranged. The athletes' beds have also been ordered and are under construction, with more than 2,000 beds. They are expected to be completed and available for use before the 20th.

Dining Hall: The location of the dining hall is in front of the dormitory and is quite spacious, accommodating more than 200 seats. Therefore, each meal can be served to everyone at the same time. The equipment in the hall focuses on sanitation and aesthetics.

(3) Propaganda Team Officially Established

In order to facilitate the news media's coverage of news and to concentrate propaganda materials, the association has established a propaganda team under the general affairs section, appointing Wu Jianying as the team leader, and Lou Weihong and Xu Tailai as team members. Ball Game Court Completed 106

Seven or eight hundred Chinese and foreign spectators

Chu Minyi Personally Attends Performance

Chu Minyi, an alternate member of the Central Supervisory Committee, is enthusiastic about sports and is especially good at Taijiquan. He has invented various sports equipment such as Taiji push-hand sticks, which are ingeniously crafted and exquisitely used, and are well known to the world. Recently, he invented the ball game as a unique sport in our country's sports world. It has been in preparation for three or four months and has been successful. Yesterday, the opening ceremony of the ball game court was held, and Chinese and foreign celebrities were invited to visit. Seven or eight hundred guests arrived. The details are as follows:

Ceremonial Arrangement: The entrance of the playground of the Sino-French Industrial School is hung with two large flags of the party and the country, and the horizontal plaque reads "Opening Ceremony of the Ball Game Court." The ball game court is built in the southwest corner of the playground. The court is a circle with a diameter of 60 feet, with a flat area of 10 feet in diameter in the center, covered with bamboo mats. Bamboo poles are used to form a circular bamboo frame around the perimeter, with a high and low perimeter. The two sides are woven into a disc shape with bamboo poles 25 feet long. The height of the edge is 4 feet 5 inches. A 2 feet 5 inches high bamboo railing is surrounded on the edge, with small party and national flags hanging. Two large bamboo balls with a diameter of about 4 feet are placed in the center of the court. In addition to the ball game court, various equipment such as Taiji push-hand root and push-hand copper balls are also arranged in the center of the court. The guest seats are set up in the east of the court, surrounded by small party and national flags, and the arrangement is very grand.

Chinese and Foreign Guests: Yesterday afternoon, around 3:00 PM, Chinese and foreign guests continued to arrive. Central dignitaries such as Cai Yuanpei, Li Shizeng, Wang Zhengting, and Ding Chao attended the ceremony. Former Minister to Belgium Wang Jingqi, Railway Department Vice Minister Li Zhaohuan, Navy Dispatch Office Military Affairs Bureau Director Ren Guangyu, Central National Health Institute Director Zhang Zhijiang's representative Tang Fansheng, and Shanghai celebrities Lai Gongchuo, Di Pingzi, Wang Xiaolai, Taijiquan expert Wu Jianquan, and foreign guests, including the consuls of France and Belgium in Shanghai, and others, a total of seven or eight hundred people, were warmly received by Chu Minyi, Dai Chunfeng, Wu Tiankan, and others.

Performance: At 3:00 PM, the opening ceremony of the ball game court began. Chu personally performed the ball game. Chu stood in the center of the court, first using his hands to rotate the two balls against each other and push them upwards, then kicking them with his feet and blocking them with his body. His whole body and limbs moved and used the two balls according to the rotation of the balls, rising and falling and spinning on the frame. The audience applauded and admired him. After the performance, Chu and Taijiquan expert Wu Jianquan and others performed push-hand balls and push-hand sticks, which were all powerful. At the same time, filmmakers and photographers of guests' camera boxes were very busy. Around 5:00 PM, refreshments were served and the guests dispersed.

Guest Performances: There were many famous Chinese martial arts masters among the guests. Chu personally invited famous masters to perform martial arts, including President Jiang's bodyguard Liu Baichuan's single sword, double sword, and Taijiquan expert Wu Jianquan's Taijiquan, Wu Jianquan's eldest daughter Miss Wu's Taiji sword, martial arts master Liu Desheng's double sword, Tong Zhongyi's double halberd, Tong Jiaxiang's grandson's crutches, the flashing swords and shadows were amazing. Then Chu Minyi and Jin Xiufeng's Taiji duiquan, Tong Zhongyi and Tong Jiaxiang's wrestling, the disciple was twice wrestled to the ground by the teacher. Wu Jianquan and Jin Xiufeng and Guan Jiesan Ma Yueliang Xu Zhiyi's Taiji push fist Wu old gentleman seemed to use no effort, but Jin Guan Ma and others fell several feet away every time, only Xu Jun resisted effectively and was not pushed down, but it was already difficult. The audience applauded incessantly.

Foreign Propaganda: Chu told people that when he went to Belgium to attend the Expo, he would bring the Taiji push-hand ball and push-hand stick for display, and would also take them to the International Sports Federation meeting in Switzerland for propaganda to provide for the hobby of sports enthusiasts around the world.

East China Intercollegiate Basketball Tournament: Shanghai University Wins the Championship 107

Yesterday's Victory Over Soochow University

55 to 27

The East China Intercollegiate Athletic Association basketball championship has concluded yesterday. Shanghai University first lost to Ginling, then defeated Soochow yesterday to win the championship. Ginling lost to Shanghai University but defeated Soochow, ranking second. Soochow lost both games and was relegated to last place.

The game between Shanghai University and Soochow University yesterday began at 4 PM. Referee: Smith. Shanghai University started strong, scoring ten consecutive points. Soochow University did not score until a few minutes before the end of the first half when Soochow’s momentum suddenly increased, achieving several points, but it was fleeting and did not last. At the end of the first half, Shanghai University led with a score of 24 to 12.

After the break, Shanghai University took advantage of their momentum, and their performance became even stronger. Not only did the substitution of players not diminish their strength, but it intensified their efforts. Sun Zemin repeatedly made great contributions, and A Liang's long shots were effective. Soochow’s defense was flawed, and their shots were inaccurate, making the situation increasingly dire. As a result, Shanghai University won with a score of 55 to 27.

Far Eastern Games: Japan Actively Prepares 116

(1) Confidence in Winning Championships

Japan has long been preparing for the 9th Far Eastern Games. Athletes for various competitions will be selected successively. Japan has always been inferior to China and the Philippines in volleyball and basketball tactics. Therefore, athletes for these two sports have been specially announced in advance and are currently undergoing intense training in the hope of winning and ending China and the Philippines' dominance in the Far Eastern Games. The enthusiasm of the Japanese is truly astonishing. According to general speculation, Japan will still be the winner of this year's games because Japan is sure to win in four out of the eight sports, namely track and field (five and ten events), baseball, and tennis. As for volleyball and basketball, Japan also has the hope of winning. Only in soccer may they not be able to defeat China, and in swimming, they may not be as good as the Philippines. But for the rest, they have a great chance of winning. The championship of each track and field competition always belongs to Japan.

Track and field is the most important of the eight sports, and strong countries and races pay attention to track and field because it represents the spirit of a strong country. Victory can greatly show the strength of the nation. Local News

Tree Planting Ceremony Held on Premier Sun's Death Anniversary 118

Location: Civilian Residences on Quanjia'an Road

The Two-Roads Bureau also held a public memorial ceremony and tree planting in Nanxiang.

The 12th of this month is the fifth anniversary of the death of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the Premier of the Chinese Nationalist Party, and also the Arbor Day stipulated by the central government. In addition to holding a memorial meeting at the Shanghai Business Association at 9 AM, the Municipal Executive Committee has also issued a notice specifying that a tree planting ceremony will be held at 1 PM at the civilian residences on Quanjia'an Road, about two li east of the park shooting range on North Sichuan Road, and designating this location as the tree planting site for each district branch. Seedlings have been obtained from the tree planting ceremony preparation committee. It is reported that the Municipal Executive Committee has ordered each district party department to instruct their respective branches to send three representatives to plant trees, expressing the Premier's intention to benefit the people.

All personnel from both roads attending are required to wear black armbands to express their grief and solemnity."

The original letter stated: "We received a letter from the Central Army, Navy, and Air Force Prison Training Class, stating that the Headquarters Military Law Department approved a public letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs regarding the visit of your class's students to foreign prisons in Shanghai. We have already copied the original letter and sent it to you for your reference. Now, we have received another letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stating that the Shanghai Office, based on information from the Provisional Court, will allow students to visit in shifts of six. We are responding accordingly and sending the original documents for your review. Please reply so that we can forward the response and inform them. The students of our class are scheduled to travel from Nanjing to Suzhou on the 6th of this month, and from Suzhou to Shanghai on the 8th. On the 10th and 11th, they will visit the foreign prisons and detention center of the Public Works Department in Shanghai. In addition to reporting this, we are writing to your office to request your assistance in making arrangements in advance and sending someone to guide them. We have previously received a reply from your court stating that students will be allowed to visit in shifts of six. This has been reported to the Ministry and forwarded. Now, Director Hu Zhikang of the training class is leading eighty students to Shanghai. If only six people are allowed to visit each day, it will take more than ten days to complete the visits for eighty people. Moreover, the visitors have other work in Nanjing and cannot stay for a long time, and staying in a hotel would be very costly. Could it be possible to arrange for visits in two shifts, morning and afternoon, with six people in each shift? In addition to our office assigning Clerk Miao Weny to accompany them, we are writing to request that you forward this request to the Public Works Department Prison and Detention Center for their consideration, to foster public goodwill."

Wang Jingqi's Opinions on the Far East Investigation Team 131

According to the Kuomin News Agency, the China Press published on March 6th about the opium situation in Anhui, and on March 9th, it published the opinions of the Far East Investigation Team, which has drawn great attention from people in the country. Minister Wang Jingqi, who struggled in the League of Nations Opium Prohibition Committee last year, is now in Shanghai. The reporter specially visited him to inquire about the real situation. According to Minister Wang, the Far East Investigation Team stated that the League of Nations could not accept the proposals of the Chinese delegation for two reasons. The first point was that China's request to send personnel to participate in the investigation team could not be accommodated by the League of Nations because if China was allowed to participate, other countries related to opium would also demand to participate. The second point was that China's request to investigate morphine at the same time should be handled by the newly established Central Supervisory Department of the League of Nations, so it could not be allowed. These two points are somewhat different from the facts. First, when the Council of the League of Nations was meeting, I did propose the idea of Chinese participation in the investigation team. Later, the general consensus was that personnel from countries not involved in opium should be engaged in the investigation. At that time, we stated that if the investigation team could expand the scope of investigation to other regions and items, our representative could suggest to the Chinese government to cancel the proposal of Chinese participation. Second, the Central Supervisory Department was not yet established at that time. Even if it had been established, the department was produced according to Chapter 7, Article 19 of the 1925 Geneva Convention, which China and the United States, who have suffered the most from foreign toxins, have not signed. Moreover, investigating morphine does not conflict with the duties entrusted to the Supervisory Department by the Convention, nor is it repetitive. For example, the team is now specifically investigating opium, which does not conflict with or repeat the Supervisory Department's duty to collect opium statistics according to Article 23 of the Convention. Therefore, based on this reason, abandoning morphine without investigation is really unsatisfactory to the Chinese people. At first, they opposed us, only saying that it was because it cost too much money and there were economic problems. That's why I said in Hangzhou on October 15th in a conversation with the Kuomin News Agency that "funding cannot be a problem, because the production of drugs is mostly in Europe, and transportation is convenient, arriving in the evening after departing in the morning, without spending too much money. Japan is the producer of drugs outside of Europe. Now that the Far East Investigation Team has arrived in the Far East, if they investigate the opium seedlings in Japan within the scope set by the meeting, it seems that they are clearly aware that Japan does not produce opium seedlings, and are just making a formal observation. As for the situation in which Japan produces a large amount of drugs, they are ignoring it, which really puzzles Chinese people who are enthusiastic about resisting drugs." But we hope that everyone understands that the Chinese people are in principle consistent with the League of Nations, only the methods are different. Fortunately, over the past year, all parties have become more aware of the harm of morphine and other products, and restriction measures will be drafted soon, which is very gratifying. As for the China Press reporter's statement that Chinese representatives said many face-saving words at the Geneva Opium Prohibition Conference, it is really not worth a smile. Such ridicule from reporters outside of China is really regrettable for us to hear. Chinese representatives at the International Opium Prohibition Conference have two roles: one domestic and one international. They themselves also know that due to various reasons of internal strife in the country, the disaster of opium has not yet been eradicated, which is a cause of infinite grief. Therefore, they have also expressed countless sincere opinions domestically. But no matter how severe the opium disaster is, it is only the Chinese harming themselves. We have not massacred people from other countries. We should do it ourselves. In the international arena, China has suffered harm from foreign toxins, which is evidenced. Chinese representatives, of course, cannot but rise up against the excessive production of morphine. That's why I said before that "if the country cannot use honest and sincere means to immediately prohibit opium, then we will only feel sorry for ourselves and can no longer resent others. This is a matter of China's own side. On the other hand, if foreigners do not restrict drug factories, do not comply with the Hague Convention, and still rely on the power of unequal treaties to harm our people at home and abroad with drugs, then foreigners are sorry to the Chinese people, and we cannot blame the Chinese people of today and tomorrow for being eternally heartbroken." Chinese diplomats' love for the country, truth, and justice is no less than that of any country. No matter what country a person is from, if they are in the position of representing China at the Opium Prohibition Conference, they cannot have a second attitude. In the past, when new Chinese diplomats wanted to protect China's sovereignty, they were not subjected to various attacks from foreigners. Unexpectedly, today, the attitude of the Chinese representative to the Opium Prohibition Committee has been directly damaging the personal dignity and indirectly damaging the prestige of the country he represents. But if the attitude of the Chinese representative can awaken the world to the harm of foreign toxins to China and to our Asian nations, we ourselves are also very honored. The above is my personal opinion, but I think the views of the Chinese government and the people of the whole country will not differ much.

Silk Industry Improves Silk Packaging and Silk Unpacking Procedures 133

Effective April 1st

The Shanghai Silk Mill Association has discussed and finalized measures to improve silk packaging and silk unpacking procedures. Yesterday, it sent letters to various silk mills, requesting them to take note and implement the measures. The letter stated: "Our silk mill colleagues have traditionally used oil paper and white sheets to wrap silk packages, with a thin hemp bag as the outer layer, tied with ropes. This method is not only wasteful but also fails to show proper respect. Based on the meeting of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Mill Industry Association, we have formulated improved measures for silk unpacking procedures and silk packaging. Starting from April 1st, all silk packages will be replaced with new-style canvas bags. All hemp bags, ropes, oil paper, etc., should be abolished immediately. To prevent theft along the way, German steel pliers will be used to crimp lead seals. In the future, when silk is sent to the raw silk inspection office for inspection, only silk packages with intact lead seals will be accepted. Therefore, the improvement of silk packaging and silk unpacking procedures is essential. All our colleagues should prepare early to avoid being caught unprepared. If colleagues are unsure about the style of the canvas bags or where to purchase steel pliers and lead seals, the association has samples available for viewing. We can also assist with purchasing. German lead-sealing steel pliers, including engraving of Chinese and Western factory names, cost $8.50 each, and canvas bags cost $5.00 each. When entrusting us with purchasing, please send a list of the factory name and the number of canvas bags needed as soon as possible. As for the silk unpacking procedures, we would like to reiterate the following points, and we hope you will take note: Silk unpacking procedures: (1) When packing silk, first pack fifteen bundles of silk into the usual cloth bag, then place it into a standard canvas bag. (2) After packing, fasten the two straps of the canvas bag and insert lead wool through the holes under the copper fastener, then crimp the lead seal. (3) When unpacking silk, factory staff and the godown staff should send the silk to the foreign firm's godown and remove the lead seal on the spot to wait. After the samples are drawn, refasten and crimp the seal. (4) After the silk has passed the foreign firm's inspection, the foreign firm will notify the factory by telephone to send staff to the firm to open the seal for inspection. If there are no errors, refasten and crimp the seal according to the previous method, and allow the foreign firm to transfer it to the raw silk inspection office for public measurement. The procedures will be handled by the foreign firm. (5) The raw silk inspection office will inspect the silk packages sent by the foreign firm to see if the lead seals of the manufacturer are intact. If they are, they will be accepted; otherwise, they will be rejected. (6) After the public measurement is completed, the silk will be sent back to the foreign firm by the raw silk inspection office. The canvas bag and the samples will be retrieved by the factory's staff from the foreign firm. Since raw silk is inspected and publicly measured by both the foreign firm and the raw silk inspection office, to and from, to avoid danger in transit, all have theft insurance in accordance with the insurance regulations. If the silk package is not intact and the seal is not complete, the insurance company will not be responsible. Therefore, improving the silk package and adding a lead seal are necessary procedures after the implementation of public measurement. Please pay attention. Shanghai Silk Mill Association Committee."

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Requests Resolution of the Jiangsu Province Post-War Public Debt 134

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Jiangsu Provincial Government yesterday regarding the urgent resolution of the Jiangsu Province post-war public debt: "In the 17th year of the Republic of China (1928), the former General Chamber of Commerce, the Bankers Association, and the Money Shops Association jointly presented to the government that the Jiangsu Province post-war public debt had been in arrears for a long time. They requested that the increased price of salt in the five Huainan prefectures, which was changed to donations in the 15th year of the Republic of China (1926), be used as the fund for guaranteeing the principal and interest of the debt. After the loans borrowed by the financial circles of Yangzi and Shanghai are repaid, a new list of extended repayment periods will be created, and the doubled revenue will be stored separately in a special account. Following the example of treasury bonds, a committee will be established to manage the funds, so as to gradually repay the outstanding principal and interest, so as to demonstrate creditworthiness. On March 23rd of that year, the government issued Directive No. 413, stating that the matter had been noted and requested that the Finance Department review and forward it for further examination. To date, two years have passed, and no further instructions have been received. Bondholders have repeatedly questioned the matter at the association, and they believe that the debt with a specified fund and the debt without security should be included in the scope of resolution. Since the issuance of the debt, interest has only been paid once, and bondholders have suffered significant losses. Public debt issued in Zhejiang Province has been paid in full, principal and interest, in proportion to the amount of the debt. Jiangsu and Zhejiang are adjacent, and the measures should not be different. Please forward the request for a method to maintain the creditworthiness and avoid prolonged delays. The Shanghai Special Municipality Business Organization Rectification Committee humbly requests your consideration."

Lawsuit Filed in New Kang Ship Collision Case 135

Demanding Compensation of One Million Yuan in Losses

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's New Kang ship was sunk by the Japanese Mail Steamship Company's Ryuno Maru in Shandong last year. After repeated negotiations, no progress was made. The company has now obtained approval from the Ministry of Communications to file a lawsuit demanding compensation of one million yuan in losses. The venue for the lawsuit has also been approved by the ministry to be the Shanghai Provisional Court. The Ministry of Communications has sent a note to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, notifying the Japanese side to appear in court for questioning.

Compilation of Merchant Ship Accidents 136

He Lun Collides with Japanese Ship. Recently, Shanghai's cargo volume has been abnormally congested, and the shipping companies in Shanghai are competing to dispatch ships for loading. The Japanese ship Shimizu Maru of the American-owned Meishun Foreign Company in Shanghai loaded a large number of goods and was transporting them to Tianjin. On the morning of the previous day, when it was sailing near Gaoqiao Sand on the Huangpu River, a Dutch merchant ship, the Qimi, which was transporting goods from Europe to Shanghai, suddenly came head-on and entered the same line as the Japanese ship. At this time, the tide was rushing, and the Japanese ship Shimizu Maru tried to avoid it, but it was too late, causing the Shimizu Maru's bow cabin to be violently hit by the Dutch ship. A hole was knocked into the cargo hold of the Japanese ship, and seawater immediately rushed into the cabin. The ship's bow sank. The shipowner was shocked and, fearing that the entire ship would sink, immediately ordered the driver to drive fast and ground the Shimizu Maru on a shoal. He then urgently hired barges to unload all the ship's cargo ashore, and then repaired the damaged area. As for the Dutch ship, only the bow suffered minor damage.

Salvage of the Feichu Ship. The Feichu ship of the Sanbei Company was violently hit by the Jiangzhen military cabin ship, which was going downstream from Turtle Mountain, at noon on the 24th of last month at the Hankou riverfront. The Feichu ship was immediately broken and sank into the river. The Shanghai headquarters sent Chief Shipowner Paos to Hankou to inspect whether it could be salvaged. Yesterday, Paos returned to Shanghai and reported to the company that the Feichu could be salvaged. Therefore, yesterday, the Sanbei Company sent six technicians and a batch of workers, along with water pumps, etc., from Shanghai to Beijing, and then transferred to Hankou to carry out salvage work.

Rescue of the Baling Maru. The Baling Maru, a direct north-south liner of the Nisshin Company, encountered a reef in the waters off Nanao Island, east of Shantou, on February 28th while traveling from Guangdong to Shanghai. The Japanese warship Kaki, stationed in Shantou, immediately sailed to Nanao and sent a platoon of navy to protect the Baling Maru. The area near Nanao is a den of pirates. On the third day of the Baling's accident, a group of pirates plotted to rob the ship but were repelled by the Japanese navy. The passengers inside the ship have been transferred by the company's Lushan Maru to the shores of Shantou and Guangdong. The cargo is still trapped in the cabins. According to a telegram from the chief shipowner who went to the rescue, the seabed reef is fortunately flat, so the ship's hull has not been broken. The holes in the first and second cabins have been patched with cement, and water is currently being pumped out. Once the accumulated water is pumped out and the cement dries, it can be towed back. It is expected to arrive in Shanghai within about three weeks.

Yangtze River Route Freight Rates Increased 137

Effective from the 17th

The shipping companies on the Yangtze River and along the coast, including China Merchants, Sanbei, Hongan, Jardine Matheson, Taikoo, and Nisshin, have unanimously decided to increase freight rates on all Yangtze River routes by 15% starting from the 17th of this month due to the soaring gold prices affecting costs. For other routes to Xiamen, Shantou, Hong Kong, and Guangdong, the increase varies by company, but it is approximately 10%. Merchants have been notified of this yesterday.

Notification of Increased Insurance Premiums for Merchant Ships During Military Use 138

The Shipping Association sent a letter to its member shipping companies yesterday, stating: "Regarding the issue of increased insurance premiums for ships during military use, the Insurance Association has repeatedly sent letters to inform us, and this association has replied with amendments in accordance with the resolutions of the previous executive and supervisory committee meetings. The issue has been basically resolved. Here is a summary of the correspondence between the Insurance Association and this association: (1) The Insurance Association's letter on January 16 stated that if ships do not increase insurance premiums according to the newly set rate (0.35% per month, 0.50% for three months, 0.75% for six months, 1% per year) during military use, the insurance policy will be suspended. If no notification was given at the time, the premium cannot be refunded. (2) This association replied on January 23 in accordance with the resolution of the second joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees, stating that the annual premium should be calculated at 1%, with each month as a unit. For example, if military use is less than one month, it will also be calculated as one month, and if it is more than one month, it will be calculated on a daily basis. (3) The Insurance Association's letter on February 22 stated that the proposed increase in insurance premiums was indeed necessary due to the excessive risks of military chartering and requisition, and the increase was necessary to compensate for the risks. They could not agree with the annual increase of 1%. (4) On March 3, this association replied in accordance with the resolution of the third executive committee meeting, agreeing to change the insurance period to units of three months (i.e., additional insurance must be for three months at a time, and if the period expires and continued insurance is needed, it must still be for three months, and so on). The premium will be fixed at 2.5 yuan per hundred taels. (5) The Insurance Association's letter on March 7 stated that the measures described in this association's letter of March 3 had been submitted to the meeting on March 6, and it was resolved to temporarily follow the procedures. We hope that you will understand the past and know the results, and that in the future, if your company's ships are requisitioned for military use, you should declare the military use to the original insurance company of the ship in accordance with the measures resolved by the third executive and supervisory committee meeting of this association and pay the additional insurance premium on time to be prepared. We hope that you will pay attention to this matter."

Telegrams Sent to Unreorganized Chambers of Commerce Yesterday

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce sent telegrams yesterday to the General Chambers of Commerce and the Shanghai Special Municipality Business Rectification Committee and Guangzhou Special Municipality Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce in the locations of the provincial federations of commerce in Guangxi, Shaanxi, Xinjiang, Ningxia, Qinghai, Suiyuan, Chahar, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Guizhou, Xikang, and Rehe, stating: "This association has completed the reorganization in accordance with the law and has scheduled the first members' general meeting of the Republic of China Chamber of Commerce Federation for July 1st of this year to formulate regulations and submit them to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for filing. Notices have been sent to the established provincial and regional federations of commerce, special municipality chambers of commerce, and overseas Chinese chambers of commerce for their information and implementation. Since the federation of commerce in your province and the chamber of commerce in your special municipality have not yet been formally established, they are not included in the calculation for convening the general meeting in accordance with the approval of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce No. 7441. We are enclosing the original telegram and rules for your reference. At the same time, select member representatives in accordance with the Chamber of Commerce Law and the rules of the members' general meeting to attend the meeting on time. We would be very grateful for your cooperation."

Local News Two

Yesterday Morning, Robbery and Gunfire in the Eight Immortals Bridge Area 141

Ma Hongji's Residence on Wehrman Road

Eight Robbers Suddenly Arrived Early in the Morning

The Owner Was Handsome, and the Robbers Coveted Riches

One Robber Killed, One Wounded, One Policeman Wounded

At 7:30 yesterday morning, a major robbery suddenly occurred at the residence of the late Ma Fuqi, a native of Chuansha, at No. 183 Wehrman Road in the French Concession. Two robbers opened fire to resist arrest and were killed on the spot. A policeman was seriously wounded. Both sides fired over thirty shots, and a stray bullet grazed an old woman. The details are recorded below:

Eight robbers came to the residence of the late Ma Fuqi, a native of Chuansha, at No. 183 Wehrman Road in the French Concession. Ma was formerly a contractor for the cleaning department of the Chinese and foreign concessions. His business, named Ma Hongji, was quite wealthy and owned a great deal of real estate, making him a target for robbers for a long time. At 7:30 yesterday morning, while the maidservant went out to fetch water, eight robbers suddenly rushed in through the front door. They were all around thirty years old, of medium build, and spoke with a northern accent. Four of the robbers were armed with pistols and threatened everyone into silence. After entering the house, they stationed themselves at the door and in the reception hall to keep watch. The other four robbers hurriedly went upstairs, first taking the key to pry open the door of Ma's wife's (also known as Sister Agui) room. Upon opening it, they found the room empty (because Ma's wife had moved out and lived with her second son).

The robbers searched recklessly, and seeing that Ma's wife's room was empty, they then broke into the bedroom of Ma's eldest son, Ma Hongkui. They told the owner that they were short of funds and asked to borrow 500 yuan from him. Ma Hongkui replied, "Okay, but you must not lay a hand on me." After saying this, he took the key and retrieved the silver dollars from the iron safe as requested, handing them over to the robbers. Unexpectedly, the robbers were still not satisfied and began rummaging through the boxes and chests. They stole 1,500 yuan in silver dollars and 750 yuan in banknotes from the iron safe. They also stole a fox-trimmed fur robe, a white sheepskin robe, a gray satin-backed leather vest, and a copper basin hat from the clothes chest. They also snatched a gold watch and chain from Ma. Ma said to the robbers, "Since you have taken the silver dollars, you cannot take any more items." Upon hearing this, the robbers threw the gold watch back and snatched 35 yuan in banknotes and silver dollars from Ma's servant. Each robber hid the loot on their person and took off their own clothes, putting on the stolen fox-trimmed fur robes and other items before rushing out the door and fleeing.

The robbers resisted arrest along the way, fully laden with loot, and fled out the door. Six robbers ran south, while two robbers with guns covered their retreat. One robber wore a fox fur robe over a long gray-white cloth gown and a dark-colored vest, while the other wore a gray cloth robe. Unexpectedly, a servant named Qiao had already escaped and secretly reported the robbery to the police station at No. 309 nearby. When the robbers fled, Qiao and the police officer quietly followed behind. The two robbers with guns initially fled north into Kédì Road and headed straight east. When they looked back and saw someone following them, they immediately opened fire and fled. When they reached the intersection of Mintini Road, the two robbers fled north again. At this time, police officers from Nos. 398, 314, and other police stations rushed to the scene upon hearing the alarm and joined in the pursuit.

One robber was killed on the spot when the police sirens blared and the detectives gathered. One robber seized the opportunity to run into the YMCA building opposite Shou'an Lane on Mintini Road. The robber wearing the fox fur coat hid inside the construction site. Police officers from Nos. 398 and 31 followed in pursuit and fired a shot at the robber upon entering the site, but missed. The robber quickly ran around a pile of soil and fled to the base of the south short wall. As he was about to climb over the wall after removing his fox fur coat, the two police officers fired three shots in a row, but still missed. The robber, feeling hopeless, stood still, raised both hands, and at the same time, another bullet arrived, hitting his left chest fatally. He fell to the ground and died. A six-inch Browning pistol and 400 yuan in stolen money (all Zhejiang Industrial Bank banknotes) were found on the ground. The dead robber was then dragged out by the construction workers on the site and taken to the morgue by the staff of the Tongren Fuyuan Hall to await examination. During the resistance, there were more than a dozen construction workers on the site, all of whom heard the sound and fled to avoid being hurt. Fortunately, no innocent people were injured.

One robber committed suicide at the same time. Another robber, armed and wearing a gray robe, fled west into Wagner Road. The police officer from No. 309 relentlessly pursued him. When he reached the entrance of the Weimei Sauce Garden at No. 29, the robber suddenly fell to the ground. The police officer from No. 309 was already very close. The robber quickly raised his hand and fired a shot, hitting the police officer in the left shoulder, causing him to fall to the ground in pain. The robber, knowing that he could not escape, turned the gun and fired a shot at his own head, piercing the back of his head. Blood flowed like a river, and he fell to the ground unconscious. The detectives who arrived at the scene checked and found that he was not yet dead. They immediately sent him and the police officer to the Guangci Hospital on Kim Shenfu Road for treatment. It was reported that the robber's injuries were very serious and he was in critical condition. The police officer, although seriously injured, was not in life-threatening danger.

Bullet marks were everywhere. During the resistance along the way, both sides fired over thirty shots, leaving bullet marks everywhere they passed. According to a detailed investigation, a piece of glass was broken on the south-facing window of No. 44 Mintini Road, and a hole was created on the cement floor in front of No. 46. A piece of glass was destroyed on the west-facing window of the Hengfaxiang Rice Store at No. 7 Wagner Road. A stray bullet grazed the forehead of Bao Chenshi, an old woman from Ningbo (75 years old) in front of the Lishunxing Cotton Store on the second floor at No. 44, who was later sent to Baolong Hospital for treatment. It was reported that the injury was very minor. As for the south side of the YMCA, there were many bullet holes and obvious bullet marks.

A detailed investigation was conducted after the incident. The police station learned that the patrol chief immediately ordered detectives to investigate the owner's house and the construction site of the YMCA. In the owner's house, they found the long clothes that the robbers had taken off. They also found the stolen fox fur coat on the road. Two pistols were also found near the robber's body. They took everything back to the police station. On the one hand, the police station ordered detectives to send the injured police officer and Bao to the hospital for treatment separately. On the other hand, the robber's body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall morgue. In the afternoon, the Criminal Division of the French Police Station reported to the French Court. At 2:30, Judge Zhu of the court came to the morgue to examine the body of the unnamed robber and confirmed that he had died from gunshot wounds while resisting arrest. He ordered that photos be taken and the body be collected by the court. On the one hand, the patrol chief ordered all patrolmen to pay close attention and strictly investigate the robbers to bring them to justice.

The Local Court Tries the Jiangwan Counterfeit Money Case 142

Wang, a Sixty-Year-Old Unmarried Woman

Said to the Judge, "Have the Virtue of Preserving Life"

The Judge Said, "It's Too Late to Regret"

"It's Difficult to Avoid Punishment Even if You Say Good Things"

The Bao Patrolman of the Laozha Police Station in the Public Concession, after arresting counterfeit banknote criminals, discovered that the organization was located in the Shenjiahang and Zhaojiahang areas of Jiangwan. He then joined detectives from the Public Security Bureau to go to Jiangwan, where they separately cracked the cases. They found four machines in the cellars, as well as printing plates and 30,000 to 40,000 yuan in counterfeit banknotes. They immediately arrested the landlords Shen Ada, Shen Lu, Wang, Wang Zhao, and others, and brought them to the Provisional Court. The prosecutor has filed a public prosecution, citing the crime of counterfeiting currency. Yesterday morning at 10:00, Judge Shen Bingle opened the court to hear the case. The Clothing of Reactionary Youths Worth Noting 143

Ye Ying Wears a Special Long Gown

The Buttons Are on the Left Lapel of the Gown

Is It What Confucius Called "Wearing the Left Lapel"?

All the Defendants Were Separately Escorted Away

On the occasion of the March 8th Women's Day, the youths arrested by the Public Concession police at Nanjing Road, Fujian Road, and North Shanxi Road Bridge were all sent to the Provisional Court yesterday morning, and the police lawyers filed separate charges. Among them were Lu Jinchu from Hubei, Zeng Baideng from Anhui, and Sun Shuguang from Fujian, all of whom were charged with distributing reactionary flyers and shouting reactionary slogans. The buttons of his long gown were usually on the right side of the gown, but Ye's were on the left side. Therefore, the police lawyer requested the judge to pay attention to his clothing, saying that Ye's wearing such an abnormal dress actually contained the meaning that he was a leftist.

Left the School the Day Before Yesterday, Destination Unknown

A Suicide Note Said He Would Throw Himself into the Huangpu River

French Automobile Adventurer Passes Through Shanghai to Japan 145

Ms. D'Artal and Mr. Lecorre

The Shanghai Times reported that Ms. D'Artal and Mr. Lecorre of France, who are well-known in the French art and sports circles, recently drove a car on a northern global tour. They arrived in Shanghai on the President Madison last Friday and then boarded the original ship to cross the East Sea, intending to drive around the scenic spots in Japan. Ms. D'Artal is beautiful and excels at singing. Mr. Lecorre is a 24-year-old youth who is internationally known for his excellent driving skills. In 1927 and 1928, he crossed the Sahara Desert with a certain person and reached Paris, setting a world record for long-distance driving. This time, he left Paris on July 9 of the previous year, passing through Italy, Yugoslavia, the Khazars, Turkey, Syria, Birobitz, Damascus, Baghdad, India, Vietnam, and other places. Although he did not encounter any dangers along the way, he had endured a lot of hardships and had traveled through uninhabited areas. The car he used was equipped with a La-Z-Boy engine, and the car was specially built in France.

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Cracks Down on Illegal Business Operations of Well-Drilling Companies 151

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities has been conducting registration of well-drilling companies in accordance with the city's water supply rules since September of last year. It was found that the Zhonghua Well-Drilling Bureau has been operating in the urban area. The registration notice was sent to them, and a letter was also sent urging them to register. However, the company delayed and ignored the notice. The registration deadline has long passed, but they still have not complied with the regulations. Recently, the bureau sent personnel to investigate and found that the company was still operating with a county license. The police from the Second Sub-District of the First District of the Public Security Bureau were requested to detain the accountant. The bureau believes that the company's refusal to register and its unauthorized operation in the city are deliberate violations of the regulations. Therefore, it sent a letter to the Municipal Public Security Bureau requesting that it be dealt with in accordance with the regulations. If the company wants to continue operating in the city after paying the fine, it must be ordered to pay a deposit to the Bureau of Public Utilities to complete the registration and then be refunded.

Robbers Injure People at Qichang Factory in Pudong 153

Han Fengjiang from Shandong, 41 years old, moved to No. 2 in the vicinity of the Qichang Stack Foundry in Pudong around July or August last year. He had no wife, and the four people living with him at home were his brothers and nephews. Han had no permanent occupation. His daily life depended on lending money at high interest. The night before last, Han's four family members were playing at the neighbor's house and had not returned. Han was left alone at home. At 11:00 p.m., three robbers suddenly came. One robber was armed with a pistol. At that time, Han's door was not bolted. The robbers rushed in, pulled out their pistols, and forbade Han from making any noise. They then searched for loot and stole a total of 52 yuan in cash, 26,000 copper coins, a fake wool crepe mandarin jacket, a felt hat, and a pair of straight wool crepe shoes. They fled out with the loot. Han, witnessing the scene, was heartbroken and shouted "Catch the robbers!" This angered the robbers, who raised their guns at Han's body and said, "I'll send you off!" After saying this, he pulled the trigger and fired. There was a loud bang, and Han's left leg was hit. The bullet was deeply embedded and did not come out. Han fell to the ground after being injured, bleeding profusely. When his family members heard the gunshots and rushed over, they saw what had happened and immediately reported the matter to the Third District Police Station and requested an arrest. Patrol Chief Shen of the police station supervised the police to rush to the scene to pursue the robbers, but the robbers had already gone far away. He then helped Han's family members carry him to the Pudong Hospital for treatment. However, because the bullet had not penetrated and the hospital was not equipped with bullet-extraction instruments, he was transferred to Tongren Hospital for treatment.

Zhou Qinzhen Sues for Divorce 154

Zhou Qinzhen, a woman from No. 3 Zhongxing Lane, Zhongshan Road, Zhabei, recently hired lawyer Yuan Jingtang to file a divorce lawsuit with the Local Court. She stated that she had married Xi Zhongfang and had four children. However, her husband neglected to provide for her, so she had no choice but to request a divorce and to request the return of the clothes and accessories taken by the defendant. She also stated that after marrying into the family in the past, she learned that the defendant was addicted to wandering and did not engage in proper business. He stayed in brothels and gambling dens all day long, neglecting his family affairs. He also smoked opium and violated the prohibited regulations. After living together for several years, she suffered all kinds of hardships and blamed her fate for meeting the wrong person. She could only endure the pain and bitterness and hope that he would change his ways and start anew. Therefore, she worked to provide for the family. Recently, he became even more excessive, secretly cohabiting with a prostitute and producing an illegitimate child. He pawned all her clothes and accessories to provide for his mistress. Such a family was no different from hell. On October 21 of last year, the defendant was willing to vow to repent, but before the ink was dry, he became even more absurd than before, wanting to push the plaintiff into an abyss of suffering from which she could never recover. Knowing that the defendant would never repent, she would never escape the sea of ​​suffering. Having such a husband, how could she grow old together? Therefore, she pleaded to be granted a divorce in order to save herself from the dire situation. A court hearing was held, and the official ordered an out-of-court settlement. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu held another court hearing. The plaintiff briefly stated the previous situation and also stated that the defendant was willing to pay 30 yuan per month, but that was just talk. The defendant Xi Zhongfang testified that he was 31 years old, from Shanghai, and engaged in the cotton yarn business, living at No. 64 Qipu Road. He stated that he was willing to pay 30 yuan per month. The defendant's father, Xi Renzhang, testified that Xi Zhongfang was his son and that he and his daughter-in-law had always been on good terms. The son and daughter-in-law had moved out to live separately for several years. The interrogating official then asked prosecutor Li to come to the court to express his opinion. The interrogating official then instructed that the debate be concluded and that a verdict be issued on the 14th. The court was then adjourned.

Unreliable Fellow Villagers 155

The Naive "Three-Stupid" Is Not So Stupid

Long Yingzi Sold

Shi Dianchun, a native of Jianxinghua, 34 years old, made a living by farming in his hometown. He had a daughter named Long Yingzi, 15 years old, who was quite beautiful. Having long heard of the prosperity of Shanghai, he planned to visit. On the 20th of last month, he took his daughter by boat to Shanghai and stayed at the home of his friend Luo Tianbang. Luo was also from Xinghua and ran a pancake shop at No. 41 Xin Street in the Nanshi area. Luo had a younger brother named San Daizi (Three-Stupid), who was 32 years old and worked as a porter on the docks. Seeing Long Yingzi's beauty, San Daizi suggested to Shi that he marry her off to a friend. Shi refused. On the 2nd of this month, Luo and his brother San Daizi suddenly invited Shi Dianchun to go sightseeing along the Huangpu River. They said that it was inconvenient to bring Long Yingzi along because she was a young girl, so they should leave her there. Shi agreed. After the three of them left, San Daizi suddenly said he had urgent business and had to go to a friend's house, so they parted ways. Around 5 p.m., Luo Tianbang and Shi Dianchun returned from their outing, only to find San Daizi sitting at home alone. Long Yingzi was nowhere to be found. They urgently asked San Daizi, who feigned ignorance. Shi was extremely anxious about his missing daughter and searched everywhere for days without success. Until yesterday, someone told him that the Luo brothers had deliberately deceived him because he was a naive villager. They had tricked him into leaving first, then San Daizi returned home under the pretext of having an errand, lured his daughter out, and sold her off. Shi was furious upon hearing this and immediately turned the Luo brothers over to police officer Cheng Jie at the 31st guard post. They were taken back to the 1st Precinct, 1st Substation, and temporarily detained to await a clear investigation and further handling.

Girl Steals Silver Dollars 156

Accuses Victim of Stalking

Bribes Police with One Dollar

Chen Zhongkang, 19 years old, a local, runs a Lukaochien meat shop in Dongjiadu, Nanshi. Yesterday around 5 p.m., a girl, about 10 years old, came to the shop and said that the Wang family at Dashenchang Cigarette Paper Shop at the corner asked her to invite him over for lunch. Chen, hearing this, remembered that Dashenchang was indeed an acquaintance, but he had never seen this young girl before, so he was suspicious and politely declined. The girl lingered in the shop for a good while before leaving without saying goodbye. Chen noticed that eight silver dollars on the counter had disappeared. Knowing that the young girl had stolen them while he was distracted, he immediately chased after her and grabbed her. He searched her and found the stolen money. Considering her young age, he let her go. When Chen returned to the shop and counted the money, he found that one dollar was missing. He chased after her again, but the girl had already taken a rickshaw heading north. When she reached near Wangjia Wharf, the girl looked back and saw someone chasing her. Realizing something was wrong, she got out of the rickshaw and reported to police officer Chen Kesui at the 5th guard post that someone was stalking her. The police officer, acting on the report, detained Chen Zhongkang. After learning the facts, the girl took out the remaining stolen dollar from her shoe and gave it to the police officer, begging him to let her go. The officer refused and took both of them to the 1st Precinct, 1st Substation. During preliminary questioning by the station chief, the girl identified herself as Wu A'mei, 15 years old, from Tongzhou. Her father's name was Zengfu, and he ran the Wansheng Teahouse outside the Ximen (West Gate) of Shanghai. She said, "My father loves me very much and sent me to school for many years. However, in recent years, my father suddenly began to mistreat me. Two years ago, I lost two gold earrings, and he ended up kicking me out. I had no choice but to stay with my aunt in Yangsi Bridge, Pudong. Today, I crossed the river to Puxi for a walk. I met a local named Shen Rurong in Xiaonanmen. He was an acquaintance because he often drank tea at my family's teahouse. Shen instructed me to use this method to steal silver dollars from the meat shop." The station chief ordered that she be temporarily detained for investigation and further handling.

Concurrent Sentences for Injury and Adultery 159

Ye Zhiqing Takes Wife Home

No More Abuse Allowed

Ye Zhiqing from Shaoxing and Jiang Youde were fellow villagers. Ye, hating Jiang for having an affair with his wife Chen, broke into house number 1107 on Yangzhou Road with a knife at noon on the 20th of this month and slashed Jiang's head. Jiang reported this to the Yangshupu Police Station, who detained Ye and sent him to the Provisional Court. Ye also accused Jiang of adultery with his wife Chen. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu continued the hearing. According to the police lawyer, the charge of injury against Ye Zhiqing had been proven in the previous hearing. Now that Jiang had recovered and was present, he was in the defendant's position regarding the adultery case. The court instructed Jiang Youde to stand in the defendant's box. Jiang testified that he had begun an affair with Chen last summer. At that time, Chen had repeatedly told him that she had been abused by her husband and was about to be killed. She wanted to return to her mother's home but had no one to support her. Therefore, she decided to choose an honest person to maintain her livelihood. Since he was having an affair with her, on the 2nd of this month, Ye came to his house. He was having lunch when Ye, without saying a word, pulled out a kitchen knife and slashed his head. On the morning of the incident, he was sitting on the edge of Chen's bed playing the flute and had not slept with her. Ye saw this and went downstairs, then came back at noon and inflicted the knife wound. Judge Xu asked if he knew the crime of having an affair with a married woman. Jiang replied that it was because she said she had no one to support her and voluntarily joined him. He said he did not know the law and begged for forgiveness. Chen testified that Ye wanted to kill her and swore she would never live with him again. Judge Xu then admonished the couple and immediately pronounced the verdict: Ye Zhiqing was sentenced to four months in prison for injury, suspended for two years; Jiang Youde was sentenced to three months in prison for having an affair; Ye and Chen were each sentenced to three months in prison for adultery, each also suspended for two years. Chen was allowed to be taken back by Ye Zhiqing, but he was not allowed to abuse her.

Li Ruzhang Forces Brother's Widow to Become His Wife 160

Brother's Widow Flees to Shanghai and Lives with Another Man

Major Conflict Ensues En Route

Li Ruzhang from Yancheng was nearly thirty but still unmarried. He farmed in his hometown and made a sufficient living. His younger brother Rubing met a woman with the surname He, a fellow native, last winter. She was twenty-nine years old and quite beautiful. Their love reached a boiling point, and they wished to spend their lives together. They married this spring and were extremely affectionate after their union. However, beauty is fleeting. Rubing soon fell ill and died. His wife, widowed at a young age, was devastated and considered remarrying after the mourning period. Unexpectedly, Ruzhang had evil intentions and wanted to take his brother's widow as his own wife. He arranged a hasty marriage ceremony. He swore she would not follow, seized an opportunity, and fled to Shanghai overnight. She soon met a rickshaw puller named Dong and rented a thatched house behind Guangzhao Road in Zhabei, living together as husband and wife. However, Li Ruzhang, unable to fulfill his desire, was extremely resentful. He took a car to Shanghai a few days ago, intending to find his brother's widow and take her back to his hometown to force her to be his wife. Yesterday, he visited the end of Hengtong Road and caught sight of Ms. He shopping in a nearby store. Overjoyed, he stepped forward, grabbed her, and forced her to return home. Unexpectedly, Ms. He shouted for help. A patrol officer heard the commotion and came to investigate. After learning the facts, he took them to the 4th District, 2nd Substation. The director questioned them. Li Ruzhang stated that the woman was his wedded wife and that she had eloped to Shanghai with another man. He asked for permission to take her back to his hometown. Ms. He stated that the older brother of her deceased husband wanted her to be his wife, but she refused and ran away. She was now living with Dong and would rather die than go with him. The judge ordered them to be sent to the Judicial Section for review.

Embezzlement of Silver Dollars Through Forged Accounts 161

Initial Trial Verdict: Suspended Sentence

Plaintiff Appeals

Xiong Yuanchou from Jiangbei, who worked as an accounting clerk at the Securities and Goods Exchange at No. 1 Sichuan Road, falsely created accounts from January to December last year. Using fraudulent means, he had the managing director sign them, then withdrew money from the bank for his own use. The head of the department, Chen Gongbo, discovered this and hired lawyer Zhu Sifu to sue him in the Provisional Court. The presiding judge, after investigation, sentenced Xiong to six months in prison, suspended for three years, and ordered him to repay the plaintiff 4,982 taels and 95 cents of silver and 3,869 yuan and 70 cents in silver dollars. The plaintiff was dissatisfied with the verdict and hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to file an appeal. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Qiu of the Court of Appeals, along with judges Shen and Li, held a joint hearing. First, the appellant's representative, lawyer Chen, stated the grounds for the appeal, saying that embezzlement was easier than theft and that leniency would not serve as a warning. Therefore, the suspended sentence was inappropriate. The defendant, Xiong Yuanchou, admitted to forging accounts, issuing checks, and taking silver dollars for his own use. Judge Qiu, considering the need for a detailed investigation of the case, ordered the defendant to post a 5,000-yuan bond to be released and to assist the plaintiff in investigating the accounts. The case was postponed for further hearing.

Intercepted by Water Patrol Team

A certain ship of the Dala Company in Pudong, moored in the southern Huangpu River, was approached one night last month by several bandits in a rowboat. They hooked a rope onto the ship's railing and were climbing aboard when they were spotted by an Indian guard. The bandits drew their guns and threatened him to be quiet. They forcibly removed a giant cable worth over a thousand dollars and put it on the rowboat, intending to escape with the loot. However, officers from the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team spotted them and ordered them to stop the boat. The bandits ignored the order. The original stolen cable and the abandoned rowboat were taken to the station. Team leader Xu reported the situation to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for instructions. It was learned that yesterday morning at 10:00 a.m., Jiang Yucai from Yangzhou reported to the Water Patrol Team that he was 42 years old and that the giant cable stolen from his ship was stolen by Wang Wuliuben, et al, from Zhangjiabang area in Pudong. He claimed that he was not involved and that the rowboat that was seized belonged to him. He requested that he be allowed to take it back so that he could make a living. Transshipment Industry Agrees on Delivery and Unloading Methods 171

The Bengbu City Transshipment Association of the Jinpu Railway yesterday issued a special notice to the transshipment companies of the Jinpu and Jinghu Railways. Due to the difficulties in delivering goods on the train, it was decided that all carload and less-than-carload goods imported from the north and south should be delivered at the platform. Whichever company receives the car is responsible for unloading it, and customers are not allowed to unload it themselves in order to clarify responsibilities. A special notice is issued requesting that everyone be informed.
