Free Talk

The Amazing Skill of an Apprentice at a Money Shop 185

— Holding Buddha

I once read "Supplemental Notes on Martial Arts" by Qian Jibo of Liangxi. It said that a tutor hung a sandbag in his doorway and pushed it every time he passed. Later, he used his palm to push people, and they would fall several feet away. This was the result of long practice. A guest told me about an apprentice at a money shop in Yuhang, which was quite similar to the tutor's story. This shows that learning martial arts does not necessarily require guidance from a master. A Daoist priest came to a certain money shop in Yuhang City. He was tall and sturdy, with a thick beard and an aquiline nose. His voice was like a bell, and his eyes were bright as lightning. He carried a shovel at his side and placed his alms bowl on the counter. When given copper coins, he closed his eyes and shook his head, not even glancing at them. He demanded more, doubling the amount, but still he was not satisfied. He stubbornly argued and clamored endlessly. At that moment, there happened to be an apprentice who had gathered tens of thousands of copper coins on a wooden board to prepare for storage. Hearing the commotion, he became angry. He suddenly lifted the large number of copper coins with one hand, raising them above his head as if holding a pagoda. The Daoist priest was stunned and stared intently for a long time. He then slowly said, "Tomorrow at dawn, I will wait for you outside the city for a friendly match. Do not break your promise." He then carried his shovel and alms bowl and slowly walked away. An interested observer secretly followed him for more than ten miles outside the city to a remote place. He never stopped walking. The observer noticed that the iron shovel he carried weighed no less than ten pounds, and he never switched hands. It was clear that he had great strength in his arms, wrists, and fingers. The observer returned and told the manager of the money shop about this. They were both shocked and immediately ordered the apprentice to quickly return to his hometown to avoid trouble. The next day, the Daoist priest did arrive and demanded to see the apprentice. The crowd told him that the apprentice had left early and would not be returning. The Daoist priest angrily replied, "Coward! Coward!" and then left. The apprentice had no knowledge of martial arts. He simply used to pile coins on the board every day after finishing his work. At first, there were only a few thousand coins, which he would lift with his hands. Gradually, the number increased day by day, reaching dozens of pounds, which he could lift as easily as picking up a mustard seed. He never realized how strong he had become. Unexpectedly, his one lift had startled the Daoist priest and caused him to flee.

Overseas Gleanings 186

— Dai Xiaozhong

During a moment of leisure after work, I happened to read the recent Sunday supplement of the "Times" newspaper and found an article that the people of Shanghai should definitely read. Therefore, despite my limited knowledge, I have translated it as follows:

The famous Hollywood movie magnate Van Buren and his wife once visited Shanghai, causing a sensation. Upon their return to their country, as soon as they had settled down, Hollywood reporters became very active, seeking every possible detail about Van Buren's experiences in Shanghai, leaving no stone unturned. As a result, the city's newspapers devoted considerable space to the topic. However, upon examination, the content was mostly fabricated by reporters, without any basis, simply to create sensational stories. I will cite a few examples to illustrate the absurdity.

1+1=3 The Evolution of Nature 187

When lawyer Xu Guowei first moved into his lane residence, his friend Zhang Zhenlu sent him a silver shield as a congratulatory gift. The inscription read: "1+1=3." The inscription below stated: "To brother Guowei, from your brother Zhenlu, congratulating you with mathematical calculations." Using a mathematical equation as a congratulatory message can be considered a novel approach. The literary man is playful, and Zhang's planning of auspicious occasions and mastery of mathematics are also evident here. As for the inscription being in rhyme, it is no different from a chapter heading in a novel, showing that Zhang has not abandoned his storyteller's nature. Someone asked lawyer Xu, "Regarding the phrase 'based on law, obtaining a son,' I don't know which law or clause it is based on." Xu smiled and said, "According to Zhang, the common saying of 'Grandmother's Sutra' is the law of the women's quarters. Grandmother's Sutra says that one person becomes difficult, and two people become easy."

A Laughing Matter 188

— Hai Ke

A: Do you read novels often lately?

B: I don't like novels.

A: Aren't there any good novels?

B: It's not that. It's just that the women in those novels are too romantic and don't agree with me.

Doctor: Oh dear, I made a mistake. The medicine I prescribed for you yesterday was for another patient and is completely different from your illness.

Patient: But doctor, I've already taken it.

Doctor: How do you feel after taking it?

Patient: I actually feel much better.

Girl A: He said I sing very well. I'm the best among his girlfriends.

Girl B: He probably doesn't have many girlfriends.

Doctor (examining a patient): Your body is in very bad shape. You have at least six illnesses. If you want me to treat them, the medical fees will be very high, with no discounts.

Patient: Then would it be possible to wait until I have twelve illnesses before asking you to treat me, so you can give me a discount?

Woman: You're proposing to me now, and I must explain to you that my uncle is in legal trouble due to debt.

Man: It doesn't matter. Fortunately, my father has also been arrested and taken to court because his bank went bankrupt yesterday.

1. Mr. and Mrs. Van Buren witnessed fierce street fighting between opposing forces.

2. Mr. Van Buren said that the Chinese people in Shanghai were either laundry workers or tavern owners.

3. All rickshaw pullers suffered from coughs. Corpses were piled up along the Bund, numbering hundreds each day.

4. Mr. and Mrs. Van Buren got lost while out one day and accidentally entered the Forbidden City.

Record of Using Pigeons to Transport Drugs 189

— Qiu Shui

Since the beginning, civilized countries have been exerting all their efforts to prohibit the transportation and trade of narcotics. However, the stricter the prohibition, the more ingenious the methods used by smugglers, inventing various ways to evade the law. As a result, the transportation of narcotics is becoming increasingly prevalent. I have often heard people say that as civilization advances, so do the number of cunning individuals, and the number of illegal activities also increases. Indeed, some smuggling methods involve using double-layered boxes, concealing narcotics within the layers to evade customs inspections. However, this method has been used for a long time, and the secret has become widely known, rendering it ineffective. Therefore, some people use horses, donkeys, and dogs, first feeding them narcotics wrapped in aluminum foil and then transporting them to their destination, where they are cut open to retrieve the narcotics. However, although this method is clever, the horses, donkeys, and dogs must sacrifice their lives after being used once. The procedure is cumbersome, and the profit is not high. Although such incidents have been discovered in the prosperous land of America, they are rarely seen in other countries. Chinese customs ports have other ingenious methods, and the use of animals is unheard of. Recently, I saw a shocking news item in a Western newspaper, revealing that white pigeons are being used to transport narcotics in America! Pigeons fly in the sky, high into the clouds, at great speed, making them difficult to shoot down, which is one advantage. Pigeons recognize their old homes and can return, saving manpower and eliminating the risk of getting lost, which is another advantage. Flying in the sky, they are not easily seen by state inspectors, which is a third advantage. Each transport does not harm the pigeons, and they can be used more and more efficiently, even countless times, until the pigeons die of old age, which is a fourth advantage. With these four advantages, the clever Americans have begun to imitate each other. Although the state's prohibition of narcotics is strict and the inspection is meticulous, there is nothing that can be done about it. So how is the transportation carried out? First, the pigeons are moved from their old home to a new location. Small aluminum cans are prepared, containing narcotics such as morphine, opium, and heroin. They are attached to the pigeons' legs and then released. The pigeons recognize their old homes and fly back. According to investigations, each pigeon carries narcotics worth from five to ten US dollars at the current market price. The amount carried each time depends on the distance of the journey and the pigeon's ability. This secret method has been used for a long time. It was first discovered by the government when a pigeon merchant in San Antonio reported it. The pigeon merchant had sold dozens of pairs of white homing pigeons to someone. Less than two months later, some of them flew back to the pigeon merchant's home. Upon inspection, it was found that small aluminum cans were attached to their legs, and upon closer examination, it was discovered that they contained cocaine (Note: a type of narcotic that is extremely expensive and prohibited from sale by the US government). The pigeon merchant was surprised and reported it to the police. The leak occurred because the buyer of the pigeons brought them back to raise and taught them to recognize their new nests for future use. After two months, the results were excellent, and they began using them to transport narcotics in the above-mentioned manner. Unexpectedly, some of the older pigeons did not adapt to the new nest and still remembered their old master, so they flew back. Now, the US government is discussing this issue and has begun investigating pigeon merchants everywhere, ordering them to record the addresses and names of pigeon buyers for detailed investigation. However, most of the people transporting narcotics now raise their own pigeons because pigeons are easy to raise and reproduce rapidly, and they grow up in one place, preventing them from getting lost along the way or being caught. Government officials can only lament their lack of ingenuity. Alas, the scheme is ingenious indeed! Therefore, I have written this down to warn against those who are cunning and evil.

Travel Notes from Southeast Asia (3) 190

— Linghua

Reading Ferrero's "Greatness and Decline of Rome" at night, I thought about how Greece excelled in the freedom of its city-states, but due to a lack of political unity, although it was able to resist Persia, it was eventually swallowed by the great Roman Empire. This is the drawback of being too small. The Yuan Dynasty was able to unify three continents—Asia, Europe, and Africa—but it could not last long. This is the drawback of being too large. Today, British and American colonialism have both the large and the small, which is why they are so powerful among the nations. In our Three Dynasties and the early Zhou Dynasty, the system of kings and officials dividing the people and assigning them duties also had both the large and small aspects. After the Han Dynasty, there was only the large without the small, resulting in an old and grieving nation. It is truly lamentable. Fortunately, Mr. Sun Yat-sen recently initiated nationalism, and we must also greatly advocate for self-governing groups, realize local autonomy, and begin to implement the rule of law. Then we will succeed. However, it is easy to act but difficult to know. Few people know, so ultimately the actions are ineffective. If we seek knowledge, then the spirit of the Zhou Dynasty's officials dividing the people and Mencius's system of regulating property, as well as the current laws of trade unions and the culture of self-governance and freedom of the Greeks, must be carefully studied. Thinking about this, I wanted to compile a comparison of Greek self-governance culture and Qilu culture, but I don't have the time. I will try to briefly describe its meaning.

The father of Western culture is Greece. Greece had dozens of small countries and two small city-states. The main states were Athens and Sparta. Sparta valued martial arts, similar to Qi. Athens valued literature, similar to Lu. As a result, Sparta defeated the Persian army of over 900,000, just as Qi dominated China and repelled foreign tribes. The literary Athens produced the three philosophers Socrates, Plato, and Aristotle, just as Lu had Confucius and Mencius. Military achievements are suitable for a time, while culture is passed on to future generations. The representative of the culture and system of the Chinese Three Dynasties was Qilu. The parents of the culture and system passed on to today's Western countries are Athens and Sparta. The Zhou officials, Mencius, and the systems of the Zhou Dynasty are also the lifeline of our nation's politics, education, and self-governance. However, if one does not study Greece, there is no way to compare and bring out this spirit. Therefore, I want to compile a book comparing Greek self-governance culture and Qilu culture as a textbook for general self-governance courses, which is especially urgent for overseas Chinese. If there is someone who understands Greek civilization, I hope they will do it for me. I eagerly await it.

European Correspondence (44) 191

— Liu Haisu

The Fauves (Continued)

Around 1906, the Fauvist movement arose from the inspiration of Matisse, Braque, Van Dongen, Vlaminck, Dufy, Friesz, and others. Fauvism was a reaction against the stagnation of the academic style and the reliance on rules of Impressionism and Neo-Impressionism. The ridiculed "Fauves," like the Cubists who followed, clearly saw that the scientific approach of Neo-Impressionism not only appeared technically limited but also exposed its poverty in artistic taste. This Neo-Impressionism, lacking excellence and depth, was clearly heading towards the fashionable decoration and the same boring neo-academicism as pure academicism. Therefore, the "Fauves" felt the need to open up a more profound ideal. They leaned towards something beyond the traditional impressions of nature. This view was based on the mixed objects of vision, that is, studying the objects from the already assembled and achieved objects. In other words, previous artists looked at the surface shapes of nature and depicted the so-called grandeur and beauty from them to create paintings. The "Fauves" were different. They wanted to capture an incredible emotion or mood in the depths of nature, or what they thought was in the depths of nature.

The "Fauves" opposed paintings that belittled individuality and depicted the surface shapes of nature. They believed that character and intention should not be bound by nature, but should use nature to stimulate personal inspiration. The purpose of painting was not to be a keen inventor of natural phenomena, but had other profound purposes. Because if it were only that, it would become a pitifully speculative little science, just as Renan criticized history. Therefore, the "Fauves" used their observational faculties to approach the goal of scientific analysis more closely. This observational faculty was inherited from Impressionism. They declared that in the "natural dictionary" introduced by Delacroix, they chose, needless to say, the kind of intention that was alive, and they chose the intention that came from a certain conceptual transformation of the enlarged form through the most delicate accumulation of color, to structure their works. From this point of view, they wanted to seek a new artistic achievement in the practical gains of their predecessors, which the predecessors had not discovered. Therefore, they were always concerned about striving to enrich this style so that their works would surpass those of the formally recognized masters.

In short, the "Fauve" painters wanted to find ways to implement the teachings of Cézanne, Seurat, and Renoir on the canvas. They advocated a "constructive" era, transforming the techniques of the Impressionists into an art, establishing its foundation on a new, particularly rich exploration of Neo-Classicism based on the tradition of Impressionism.

The first attempts of the "Fauves" were expressed by returning to tradition. This so-called tradition was not only in its literal sense but also in its spirit, because a work cannot exist solely on its appearance, but must also be immortalized by its soul. We can visit all the museums and discover the most abundant new research and technical principles. The works of the mixed-language era, such as the Cretan and ancient art of Greece and Byzantium, as well as the art of primitive people, Romans, and Mosatns, and even black art, can all be used to find the characteristics of that time. The "Fauves" tended towards a new spiritualization of the body, focusing on creating architectural structures, training and economizing all methods, and recognizing that this method could completely transform painting from its original sensuality into pleasurable. As for the path they took, it was through this constructive interest and the separation of lines, the transformation and reconstruction of the ideas of color masses, and finally, from the perspective of the values of form, depth, rigor, and economy, they advocated a strong and obvious "doing more with less," and opposed the rambling, redundant, and repetitive nature of Impressionism. Fauvism, with regard to nature, abandoned its external form and accepted its spirit. They did not take photographs but organized a landscape that was aroused by emotion. They did not imitate the external form of nature but were able to subtly stir the great harmony of the world.

Commercial News

Financial and Gold Market Experiences Sudden Ups and Downs 192

Different Objectives for Insiders Entering and Exiting

The Confused State is Still Difficult to Break

The Unsettled Situation Leads to More Changes

Closing Price Drops by Two Taels and Nine Mace

The Issue of Taxing Spot Silver Remains Undecided. Yesterday (Monday), the Gold Exchange operated as usual, and the gold market trended downward. However, there were sudden ups and downs, and there was no certainty. The atmosphere sometimes contained positive and negative news. There was a deficit in foreign exchange, and speculators and industry insiders sold off. The forward gold price hovered around four taels. It was still difficult for those in the industry to break the confused state. Moreover, the buying and selling objectives were different. For example, Hengxing, Shengda, Yili, and Wanxing were all pursuing gains, while Yuanmaoyong, Fuchang, Yuancheng Yong, Dadesheng, Yu Zai, and others were selling. The early market saw large bars continuing to increase, but the price contracted instead, so it was still stable, with just over 500 taels. Later, sellers rushed in, immediately breaking the 500-tael mark. By noon, the price had fallen by more than four taels. The market changes became even more intense in the afternoon, with fluctuations of as much as six taels. Initially, due to the lingering effects of the weak noon closing, it was suspected that the issue of taxing spot silver, or its implementation, had caused a psychological vacuum among the various firms, who tended to sell, causing a sharp drop to within 492 taels. The foreign exchange also showed weakness, and the market almost fell off a cliff. Afterwards, it gradually looked up again, and the momentum turned to moderation. Then, suddenly, news came that the silver tax case was difficult to resolve due to various relationships. Buyers in the market suddenly became agile, and the price rose rapidly, continuing to rise by three or four taels, finally reaching between 97 taels. Fuchang, Yu Da, Hengxing, and others all started buying, but Yuanmaoyong, Yuansheng, Bingxing, and others were still selling. As for British silver bars, the telegrams the day before yesterday had increased by eight points of a penny, but the silver price had contracted by three-eighths of a penny. Observation on the Interest Rates After the Turmoil 195

Market Overview: After the huge turmoil of the past few days, the money houses have announced the stability of the market, but the internal vitality has been completely lost and it will not be easy to recover for a while. The trading situation in the market has not been fully developed, and customers are unwilling to let go, so the collection and settlement are dull, which is reasonable. As for the interest rate, it is mostly the same as before, and the silver swap is slightly better. Although it has not risen exceptionally, it has increased with the trend, which is expected. Afterwards, it is expected that the market of more than one cent may come soon.

The result was the same as the early market, calculated as 7 mace, 2 fen, 05. (Silver Swap): The early market transfer account opened at 5 fen, and the noon market silver swap was also 5 fen. Although the internal situation was not tight, the general impact of the storm naturally made transactions impossible. The bank's drawing head was done at 5 or 6 fen in the noon market, and the small association did about 1 cent.

Decline in Wheat Market 204

Yesterday, the opening prices for the wheat market in the morning and afternoon presented a mixed picture. There were no transactions for the current month due to differing intentions between buyers and sellers. However, the April market suddenly plummeted. It is rumored that both buyers and sellers were prepared, with buyers reluctantly preparing to take delivery and sellers purchasing existing wheat from production areas along the Yangtze River to resist. As a result, market sentiment fluctuated, with prices declining gradually. However, if the drop becomes too severe, factories may potentially cause a shift in the future direction of the wheat market. Futures prices declined due to improved weather and waning investor interest, with April contracts falling by 6 points compared to the previous week, June by 2 points, July by 1 point, and August by 1 point. Spot wheat prices remained strong for factory purchases, with high-quality wheat commanding premiums of 1 to 2 points. Medium-quality wheat remained unchanged. 2,200 bags were opened, with Qingjiang wheat at 5 taels, 1 mace, and 7 fen to 2 qian, Huangqiao wheat at 5 taels, 1 mace, and 5 fen, and Zhenjiang wheat at 5 taels and 7 fen to 5 fen. These were reportedly purchased by factories such as Fufeng and Zhonghua.

Heavy Inventory of Tea in England

According to British dispatches, the British tea market has recently shown a declining trend. Inventory of black tea from India, Ceylon, and Java exceeds 300,000 chests. Since Russian buyers announced the cancellation of their previous large purchases of black tea, the market has become even more sluggish, with prices falling. While the highest quality Chinese Keemun and Ningzhou black tea are still selling well due to scarcity, mid-to-low grade tea has been greatly affected by Indian and Ceylon tea and is completely ignored.

Decline of Qifu Tea Firms 205

Due to Heavy Losses Last Year

Production of Keemun and Fuliang red tea has increased daily, and exports have been smooth and frequent. In recent years, domestic red tea operators have been tending towards these two areas, resulting in increasing mountain prices and labor costs. Since the Association for Cooperative Advancement declared its closure last year, the red tea sales market has declined greatly, with many firms closing and incurring losses. This year, most of the original tea firms in Keemun and Fuliang are taking a wait-and-see approach due to last year's setback. According to surveys by tea industry insiders in the area, Keemun tea firms have been less affected and have sufficient capital, and are preparing to open the market. Fuliang tea firms have suffered greater losses, and it is still unclear whether they will reopen. Six Huizhou tea firms have decided to enter the mountains and have leased addresses in Keemun and Fuliang. As of recently, Keemun tea firms have decreased by approximately 30% compared to the past, and Fuliang by approximately 50%. In addition, due to the sluggishness of silver in Jingdezhen and inland areas, tea firms are adopting a cautious approach and reducing the amount of financing they provide, unlike the past when they competed to provide excessive financing.

Sharp Rise in Price of 18-Gauge Black Iron Sheet

Sales of 18-gauge black iron sheet are usually greatly reduced at this time of year, and there are no special circumstances to record in the market. However, due to high prices last year, few firms ordered it, resulting in very limited imports. Recently, however, demand in the market has surged, and existing inventory has been sold out. As a result, standard prices have been rising steadily. Buyers have been actively purchasing in the past two days, with prices rising sharply from 9 taels per dan to 9 taels and 7 qian and 5 fen. Demand from Tianjin and Qingdao is strong, and local enameling factories are also taking the opportunity to snap up existing inventory. The strong trading volume is the highest among all hardware products. It is expected that the market may face shortages in a day or two. In addition, 3-foot 6-inch iron sheet has also risen to 9 taels, but trading is not as active as 18-gauge.

It is reported that most of the goods are Japanese white iron, and there are also a considerable amount of French-made and Spanish-made nails, tacks, and sheet iron.

Guangdong Province has sent personnel to Shanghai to learn silk testing techniques.

Society News

Urban Ramblings 212

Lin

(6) Life in the Nest

The Shanghai swallow has a place to perch, simply called a "nest." Life inside the nest is worth studying. Some say it's a fairyland, others say it's like a living hell. Regardless of whether it's a fairyland or a hell, the facts tell us that the two are somewhat similar. To those who are used to seeing it, this kind of place is nothing new. Mentioning the word "nest" is as plain as mentioning the word "home." However, from another perspective, the business of this nest is ultimately secretive, and life in the nest inevitably carries a mysterious color. In short, the impression that the nest gives us is a kind of morbid state in the city.

The term "nest" is not very honorable. Thirty or forty years ago, their fathers and grandfathers used "rooms" and "halls" to represent their business. At that time, the momentum was clamorous, and so-called dignitaries made friends with them. When it came to the hands of the "nest" generation, it fell into decline, very different from the past. Not only could it not glorify the family, but it had to be pointed out and monitored everywhere.

You can't find nests along the street, just like birds don't build nests in tree roots. Going up to the nest inevitably involves climbing high, almost a fixed rule, and the road is bound to be unusually circuitous. High-end nests have relatively flat roads, while mid-to-low-end nests are really narrow paths. Seclusion arises from winding paths. For example, a nest in a lane usually enters and exits from the back door. A staircase, no more than a foot wide, leads from the ground to the second and third floors in a winding manner. When entering the door, everyone can't see their fingers. After walking four or five flights of stairs, there is light leaking from the wall. At the same time, there is a whirring sound and a smell that is neither foul nor fragrant sent to your ears and nose. Therefore, the first things you encounter when entering the nest are these three things: light, sound, and smell.

Even if everyone is unfamiliar and doesn't know each other, in the nest everyone "tacitly understands each other." Going up and down the stairs and entering and exiting the doorways, they don't necessarily use gestures to express themselves, but there is naturally a kind of "tacit understanding" in their psychology. Therefore, walking on the small ladder, everyone is calm and unhurried, moving with moderate speed. Especially those who come down from the upper floors, take every step firmly. Their eyes are not blurred, and their limbs are also strong. Seeing someone going up below, whether they know them or not, they often tell the person below "walk carefully." In the midst of humming and coughing, they reveal twelve points of sympathy. Once you get to the nest, it's best not to hesitate or look around. As for rushing forward and running up in one breath, that's even more inconsistent with the logic of the "nest."

What is the first impression of a glimpse into the nest? Generally, the first thing that enters the eyes of people who enter the nest for the first time is a swirling cloud of mist, in the middle of which are immersed many wax figures, as if they have just walked into a bathhouse. Looking to the left and right again, it is as if they are stepping on someone else's bed, with long legs and short feet in all directions, reaching their own bodies. In fact, these beds are called tatami mats. Those lying horizontally on the tatami mats all turn their bodies sideways and work hard on the lamplight, swallowing and spitting out, one puff on the left and two puffs on the right, the more they smoke, the more energetic they become. On a lamp the size of a soybean, all the troubles of the world are burned clean. Presumably the first puff is the most powerful, the mouth keeps sucking, and the shoulders also follow suit. Afterwards, it gradually slows down. The most unbearable is the situation where they want to stop but can't. A haggard face, thin lips, and a tightened mouth desperately sucking, the result is that there is only air and no sound. Poor people are thinner than yellow flowers.

The furnishings in the nest are simple and straightforward, saving as much as possible. Except for a clock hanging on the wall, which has the most complicated structure, there is nothing else worth mentioning. Therefore, the air in the room is clearly cold and lifeless. If it weren't for the gentlemen on the tatami mats desperately swallowing and spitting out, creating a rich and colorful atmosphere in the room, who would want to linger there? However, in this fairyland, where day and night are indistinguishable and sunlight never shines, "fairies" often descend, creating many karmic connections. They lie across the tatami mats, stretch their arms lightly, and produce pearls with a flick of the hand, enjoying everything in the same way. The only trouble is that they have to reapply their lipstick afterwards.

In the middle of the city that never sleeps, there is work that never sleeps. The "nest" is a source of excitement, and what is produced under the excitement is the various evils of the city. Gambling should be the first thing that has a related relationship because of the nest. Therefore, in the area around the nest, there are often many gambling places, and even the upper floor is a nest and the lower floor has gambling. It's not surprising that the parlor is shaking the dice and the small room is making a nest. What is strange is that what is written on paper becomes "news." Snack shops that are open all year round and fruit stalls that do business day and night all have a direct or indirect relationship with the nest. The only difference is that the pears, oranges, apples, and other fruits sold by the fruit stalls near the nest seem to have less juice and a drier appearance. Perhaps it is because the living standards in the city are getting higher and higher every day, and the friends in the nest are oppressed by life, which has a knock-on effect on the fruit stalls.

New Dissertation Drafted by German Doctor 213

Beauty of Male Peacock Not Reflected in Female Eyes

Overturning Darwin's Theory

Yokohama dispatch: Mr. Grave, a German doctor practicing medicine in Yokohama, recently submitted a German academic dissertation entitled "A Study on the Color Biology of Pupillary Response to Short Wavelength Light" to the Faculty of Medicine of the University of Tokyo, Japan. After being approved by them, it will be recognized by the Japanese Ministry of Education and awarded the title of Doctor. The content of his research is the theory of the Darwinian school, which has always recognized the beauty of the feathers and body colors of lower animals such as black carp, identified the species' own gender, and cited it as a condition for natural selection. This theory is explained from a purely subjective standpoint. In response to this theory, Dr. Hess, Professor of the University of Munich in Germany and Mr. Grave's teacher, first studied the color recognition ability of chickens from an objective standpoint based on experiments, saying that chickens also have color vision for long-wavelength light such as red and yellow, the same as humans, but they are dull in distinguishing blue and other short-wavelength colors, or it is difficult to distinguish each color as grayscale with brightness. Mr. Grave further used experimental methods to photograph the changes in the pupil size of chickens and other lower animals when they saw various colors, and compared their sizes. For the situation described by Dr. Hess that the beauty of the male peacock is not felt by women, he further proved it with scientific experiments, saying that the beauty of the male peacock is not caused by the special beauty for the purpose of attracting females, but is the inevitable result of the physiological internal secretion and metabolism.

Osaka City Acoustics Exhibition 214

Aims to Create a City Suitable for Residence

Osaka Dispatch: In view of the prosperity of modern cities and the extraordinary development of various transportation facilities, Osaka City, considering the resulting increase in complex noises and their impact on urban life, has decided to hold an exhibition on urban acoustics at the Osaka Municipal Museum of Art starting this month on the 10th, as an aid to research. They are currently consulting various parties to exhibit related materials. The content of the exhibition includes: (1) topics related to cities and acoustics in architecture, roads, transportation, communication, industry, and music; (2) principles and reference materials, including military applications. The exhibition aims to raise public awareness, citing various facts about its impact, preventing its harmful effects, and simultaneously promoting its utility, with the goal of creating a city suitable for residence.

Japanese Initiate Regular Air Service to America 215

Aims to Cross the Pacific in Three Days and Nights

But Requires One or Two Years of Investigation Before Implementation

Tokyo Dispatch: Last autumn, Japanese individuals Hoshino Sukesada and Senaga Taro initiated the establishment of the Toa Hemisphere Air Transport Company, raising ¥15 million to commence regular air service between Japan and the United States. They petitioned the Aviation Bureau of the Ministry of Communications for permission to conduct air transport. The company plans to equip four Zeppelin-type airships to travel between Tokyo and Seattle. Flights will depart regularly from both Tokyo and Seattle every five days, crossing the Pacific in just under three days and nights. The proposed fares are ¥2,000 per passenger, ¥1 per sen for mail, and ¥177.25 per large catty for cargo, with an annual dividend of 8%. The company plans to conduct investigations for one or two years before considering implementation. According to Mr. Hoshino, he serves as both initiator and manager, with the office located on the third floor of the Aviation Building, aiming to achieve the goal.

Opening on the 20th of This Month

Includes a Panoramic Display of Naval Battles

According to Japanese dispatches, the Japan Sea and Air Exposition is scheduled to open in Yokosuka on the 20th of this month. Yokosuka is originally a naval base, so there are many exhibits, especially the panoramic display of naval battles made by the Oppama Air Group, a model of the actual live action of modern scientific warfare, with manufacturing costs alone amounting to approximately ¥20,000. In addition, rare exhibits from all over the country are gradually gathering, including twenty-one models of major battleships and aircraft carriers from various countries, made at his own expense by Manka Akimasa, a worker at the torpedo experimental department of the shipyard, and donated to the Mikasa warship. These models are approximately one two-hundredth of the actual size, with differences in the scale and dimensions of the ship type.

A Strange Tale of Shrinking Disease 217

Liang Xiongwan

'The doctor told me that, because I have this strange disease, I can live another fifty years. If this is possible, and my body continues to shrink, I might become like a little person in Lilliput. At that time, maybe I can hide in a small shoebox,' Joseph Mayott said triumphantly.

He is a soldier, a veteran who participated in the European War. The disease he suffers from is called Paget's disease, an extremely rare disease in the world. In eight years, his body has shrunk a total of nine inches, an average of one inch and one-eighth per year. Eight years ago, he was five feet seven inches tall, but now he is four feet ten inches tall. After being diagnosed by four hundred doctors, they all agreed that Mayott's disease is not only harmless but can also allow him to enjoy fifty more years of life.

The exhibition will last for two years. It has already notified foreign embassies and consulates and mailed important newspapers from various countries to prepare.

The Story of World Literature 219

(1) (4) (2) Written by John Macy of the United States, Translated by Hu Zhongchi

Chapter 38: Nineteenth-Century French Prose

As that shoulder gradually grew, that head became many heads with all sorts of power. In the early years of the same century—plus or minus a few years—novelists such as Balzac, Victor Hugo, Alexandre Dumas, and George Sand, and the critic and essayist Sainte-Beuve, were born. Balzac, the most prolific and powerful of French novelists, though he did not understand or announce his purpose until he had written many works, attempted to depict all aspects of life and called his complete works of novels 'The Human Comedy.' He did not live to complete his plan; he died at the age of fifty. 'The Human Comedy' transcends the scope of any one person, one country, or one era. However, no novelist before or after Balzac has had more right to such a universal title. He created a multitude of people who readers of any country—most of his books have been translated into all European languages—recognize as themselves and their friends and enemies, regardless of local or worldly circumstances. Balzac studied all types of Parisians, farmers, and the petty bourgeois society of small towns. Because most of his life was spent at his desk, and he was involved in the toil of undertakings that would exhaust the energy of ordinary people, it is inconceivable how he found the time to directly know so many kinds of society. The answer is that he had an unparalleled innate talent as a novelist: insight. To understand, absorb scenes and characters, make them part of himself, and give accurate details—sometimes too many details—it only took one look. His insight was strengthened by his great intellectual honesty and courage. In this respect, he resembled Scott, whom he greatly admired. Like Scott, he had to write too much to maintain a troubled life. However, he never evaded the responsibility of a writer, often working superhumanly for sixteen hours in a row, revising and polishing his works, and imbuing most of them, even extremely lengthy pages, with the inexhaustible power of immortal life. Balzac's works could practically resolve the long-standing theoretical dispute between romance and realism, which is still being conducted somewhat meaninglessly, before it even arose. For critics and novelists who investigate theories about their art, that is an interesting specialized question. Doesn't the fact that any long fictional work, regardless of its content or source material, is called a 'Roman' in the precise language of the French themselves answer that question for them? Moreover, doesn't the place practiced by the greatest French novelist, who viewed all or most of life as a romantic adventure of souls and events and spared no pain to give a true impression of facts, also answer that question? In Balzac, literal interpretation and imaginative fantasy do not conflict. Readers may see conflicts, but Balzac did not feel them. His greatness lies in the scope of his sympathy. In 'Eugenie Grandet,' he depicts a simple country girl in a narrow environment. In other books, he writes of the 'splendors and miseries' of other types of women. He was the first to incorporate the base romance of business and money into novels. In 'César Birotteau,' he used his own experiences in the world of commerce. In many, almost all, of his novels, such as 'Cousin Pons,' 'Cousin Bette,' and 'Old Goriot,' various forms of greed, miserliness, selfishness, and other hateful motives flow. Balzac is not a person who loves life in an affectionate, sentimental way. His view of life is proper and often harsh, but when it comes to young girls, it is often gentle. His attitude towards youth is generally stern. He had described 'egoists' several times long before Meredith wrote about them. He pushed the emotional life far beyond the sounds of happy couples' weddings. Marriage is just an interlude. People live on, into old age—Balzac's depictions of delusional, unpleasant, and pathetic old people are strikingly skillful. This observer of men and women has a sense of scene and circumstance, and although he is usually not a poet in style, he can approach the realm of prose poetry in 'Séraphîta,' which can be regarded as a Swedenborgian experiment in mysticism. This aspect is also thought-provoking. He is indeed a Colossus or Colosseum (Note 1), because later novelists have quarried stone from his great structure to build smaller-scale buildings.

(Note 1) The Great Circus of Rome.
